                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${\mathrm{\ \ }}{D}_{N{a}^ + } = \frac{4}{{\Pi \tau }}\ {( {\frac{{{V}_m\ {m}_B}}{{S\ {M}_B}}} )}^2{( {\frac{{\Delta {E}_S}}{{\Delta {E}_t}}} )}^2$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math>. τ, Δ<i>E</i><sub>t</sub>, and Δ<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> were the duration of the current pulse, the potential difference with the applied current, and the equilibrium potential drop before and after the current pulse, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0010_R_d1015254e1716" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The calculation results were shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0006">6e</a>, which showed that the ether-based electrolyte stores and deliquesces Na<sup>+</sup> at a higher rate than the ester-based electrolyte, indicating that the ether-based electrolyte was more conducive to the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>.</p>
            
            <p>The EIS fitting results indicated that the resistance from the SEI membrane and charge transfer (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) in the ether-based electrolyte was 10.46 and 35.46&nbsp;Ω, among which the charge transfer rate was much lower than that of the EC/ EC-based electrolyte at 410.7&nbsp;Ω (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0006">6f</a>). The linear slope of the SXL anode in the ether-based electrolyte calculated by fitting was 28.582, which was much lower than that in the ester-based electrolyte at 140.571, indicating that the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> was greater in the ether-based electrolyte.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0062_R_d1015254e1741" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Appl. Surf. Sci.">62</a>, <a href="#smll202308684-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0063_R_d1015254e1741" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The calculated Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients (D <sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup>) for ether-based and ester-based electrolytes were 2.84&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup> and 1.95&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−12</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>(Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0063_R_d1015254e1764" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>At a current density of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity of the ether-based electrolyte was 86.12&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 5000 cycles, which was higher than that of the ester-based electrolyte at 47.29&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0006">6g</a>). The sodium storage process of the ester-based electrolyte was also tested (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information). A similar sodium storage mechanism was demonstrated in the ether–ester electrolyte and the differences in electrochemical performance stemmed from the different rates of sodium storage kinetics. All of the above test experiments showed that in ether-based electrolytes, the promotion of Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics was favored.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="smll202308684-sec-0050-title">2.3 Electrochemical Performance of SXL-Based Full-Cells</h3>
            
            <p>To fully evaluate the potential of our carbon nanosheet anodes in practical applications, we assembled full cells for electrochemical testing. The choice of cathodes materials included manganese oxides,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0064_R_d1015254e1795" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - Chin. Chem. Lett.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> polyanionic compounds,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0065_R_d1015254e1800" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Prussian blue analogs et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0066_R_d1015254e1805" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - Adv. Mater.">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Finally, we assembled the sodium-ion full cell by coupling the carbon nanosheet anode to the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode(<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202308684-fig-0007">7a</a>).The electrochemical proper of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as the cathode are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information). The SXL anode was performed by pre-activated at 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> before assembling. Figures&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0007">7b–c</a> show the rate performance and constant current charging and discharging curves of the NVP//SXL full cell. Along with increased current densities of 0.5, 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the capacity of the full-cell became 217.70, 180.34, 147.90, 118.41, and 95.59&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, suggesting an excellent rate performance. The energy density of the NVP//SXL full cell was calculated for 105.93&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 230&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, and the energy density of the NVP//SXL was maintained at 54.43&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> even when the power density reached 1380&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. The cathode and anode peaks are located at 3.3 and 3.5&nbsp;V in the CV curves of the full cell (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0007">7d</a>). The two pairs of redox peaks indicate that both anode and cathode materials are involved in the electrochemical reaction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202308684-bib-0067" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202308684-bib-0067_R_d1015254e1859" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 67 - Energy &amp; Environmental Materials">67</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The green LED light can be successfully powered by an NVP//SXL full cell, which further demonstrates the full cell's excellent stability. (the inset in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0007">7d</a>). A reversible specific capacity of 105.54&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the anode) can still be obtained after 100 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>(Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202308684-fig-0007">7e</a>). Generally, this work successfully paves the way for the next-generation SIBs using dual activation-derived carbons. By coupling our anode to a sodium-layered metal oxide cathode, the energy and power of the full cell can be further increased.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202308684-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/44ab9742-ea0b-4a8b-9455-dc9f37f38f13/smll202308684-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/44ab9742-ea0b-4a8b-9455-dc9f37f38f13/smll202308684-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b310802c-8520-40eb-a771-42c7bb5ff6c1/smll202308684-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/44ab9742-ea0b-4a8b-9455-dc9f37f38f13/smll202308684-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202308684-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202308684" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performances of NVP//SXL full cells. a) Schematic illustration of full SIB. b) Rate capabilities of the full cell from 0.5 to 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> c) GCD curves. d) CV curves at 0.2&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. e)Long-term cycling performance of the full cell at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 100 cycles.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202308684-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202308684-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, we proposed a new method based on combustion activation using K<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub>/KNO<sub>3</sub> dual activation effect, forming 2D carbon materials with large specific surface areas, and applying them in sodium-ion batteries. The prepared SIB anode material exhibited a high reversible capacity of 344.44&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The synergistic effect of the salt template led to a porous structure and high content of heteroatom doping. The improved electrochemical performance was shown by ex-situ characterizations to be attributed to the action of N/S doped heteroatoms on sodium ions. A comparison of the sodium storage performance of the ether ester electrolyte showed a similar sodium storage mechanism is exhibited in both electrolytes. During the discharge process, the pyridine nitrogen is sodiated, and the Na<sup>+</sup> is formed through internal disproportionation reactions of sodium sulfonate and polysulfate complexes. The difference in electrochemical performance is attributed to the fact that the ether-based electrolyte stores and deliquesces Na<sup>+</sup> at a higher rate than the ester-based electrolyte. Importantly, the full battery composed of the SXL anode and the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode were assembled, which deliver a prominent energy density of 105.93&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 230&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>. This work could not only provide a feasible strategy for designing the heteroatom-doped carbonaceous porous structure for efficient and fast energy storage but also give a deep analysis of different storage mechanisms for Na<sup>+</sup>.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202308684-sec-0070">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202308684-sec-0070-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0080">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0090">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0100">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308684-sec-0100-title"> Synthesis</h4>
                  
                  <p>N-allylthiourea (S) was used as a precursor for self-doping and potassium sulfate (L) as a sulfur ex-source driver as well as a salt templating agent. Then an amount of potassium nitrate (X) was added as an activator. The above materials were dissolved in 100&nbsp;mL of deionized aqueous solution by magnetic stirring for 4&nbsp;h. The solution was frozen at −20&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h, freeze–dried at −45&nbsp;°C, and then calcined at 700&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h at 5&nbsp;°C&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> to prepare the porous carbon materials. The resulting product was washed with hydrochloric acid and deionized water, dried at 80&nbsp;°C for 24&nbsp;h, and designed as SXL-x (<i>x</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;3, 4, 5, 6, 7.5, <i>x</i> is the molar mass of potassium nitrate). S-5, SL, and SX-5 were obtained under similar preparation conditions to compare the role of each salt template at <i>x</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;5.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0110">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308684-sec-0110-title"> Material Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The morphology of the porous carbon was characterized by field emission scanning electron microscopy (SEM, FEI Inspect-F, Finland) equipped with energy disperse spectroscopy (EDS) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM, TA Talos F200S). Their surface chemistry was detected by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, AXIS Ultra DLD, Krato) and an Al Kα ray source. The X-ray diffraction patterns were collected by a diffractometer (XRD, Ultima IV) using a Cu Kα X-ray source at 40&nbsp;kV with a scanning rate of 5°&nbsp;min<sup>−1</sup> from 10° to 80°. Raman spectra were collected at 50–4000&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup> using a Raman spectrometer (HR Evolution) with a test wavelength of 532&nbsp;nm. An automated specific surface and porosity analyzer (Micromeritics ASAP 2460, N<sub>2</sub> at 77K. Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) method) was used to analyze the surface area and pore structure. In situ thermo–gravimetric analysis-infrared spectroscopy (TG-IR) measurements were conducted by Mettler Toledo TGA 2 coupled with Thermo Scientific Nicolet iS50.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="smll202308684-sec-0120">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="smll202308684-sec-0120-title"> Electrochemical Measurement</h4>
                  
                  <p>Negative electrode sheet preparation by the mass ratio of 7: 1.5: 1.5 ratio, the preparation of porous carbon, binder (polyvinylidene fluoride), and Li 90 mixed, supplemented with the appropriate amount of solvent N-methyl pyrrolidone (NMP) ultrasonic 3&nbsp;h, became a uniform slurry and dropleted on top of the metal plate, and then placed in a vacuum drying oven at 80&nbsp;°C after 12&nbsp;h drying, each piece of the electrode sheet had 0.6&nbsp;mg of active material.</p>
                  
                  <p>The prepared negative electrode sheet was assembled to form a Coin-type (CR 2032) half-cell using sodium metal as the counter electrode and glass fiber membrane (Whatman, GF/D) as the diaphragm. For electrolyte selection, 1&nbsp;<sub>M</sub> sodium bis (fluorosulfonyl)imide (NaFSI) in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DEGDME) was used as the ether-based electrolyte, and 1&nbsp;<sub>M</sub> NaFSI in a mixture of ethylene carbonate (EC) and diethyl carbonate (DEC) as the ester-based electrolyte in a volume ratio (1:1) for comparison.</p>
                  
                  <p>In the full cell, in which commercial sodium vanadium phosphate (Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>) was used as the cathode material, the mass ratio of sodium vanadium phosphate to anode carbon was 4:1. Constant-current charge/discharge (GCD) and constant-current intermittent titration technique (GITT) tests were carried out using a NEWARE multichannel battery test system with a half-cell voltage range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V (relative to Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) and a full-cell voltage range of 1–3.6&nbsp;V. For GITT test, a series of current pulses at 0.05&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 30&nbsp;min followed by 60&nbsp;min relaxation intervals was used. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) was performed on an electrochemical workstation (GAMRY) at scanning rates of 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> over a voltage range of 0.01–3&nbsp;V (relative to Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests were performed in the frequency range of 100&nbsp;kHz to 0.01&nbsp;Hz on an electrochemical workstation (CHI660E).</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

        <script type="text/javascript" nonce="2041d4dd1baf4d7b98cc585d4780e267">
    window.addEventListener('load', () => {
        document.querySelectorAll('.admin-bar-popup-menu ul li')?.forEach(function (li) {
            const anchor = li.querySelector('a');
            if (anchor && anchor.textContent.trim() === 'Edit Access Denial') {
